# Night Shift Changelog

Newest first. One entry per cycle. The loop appends here; you read it over coffee.

## 2026-06-23T10:38Z — PASS — partnerships-near-alert-capture
- Pages: /partnerships/near/[icao] (every airport's "aircraft partnerships near {airport}" page, e.g. /partnerships/near/khwd, /partnerships/near/kpao)
- What: **The "aircraft partnerships near {airport}" pages now have a "Get alerts for new {ICAO} area listings" email box** — the same low-friction, no-account-needed capture box the partnership make/state hubs and the for-sale (aircraft) pages already show. Until now a visitor on, say, *Aircraft partnerships near Hayward Executive (KHWD)* — a high-intent geo SEO page — had no way to be notified when a new nearby co-ownership listing appears; they'd have to keep checking back. The box sits just below the listings (above the cross-links), reads with partnership-appropriate wording ("we'll email you when a new KHWD area partnership is listed"), and feeds the same confirmed double-opt-in pipeline shipped last week (so it's safe and sendable the moment the human adds a Resend key). No visual change to any other page.
- Goal: feature depth / list-building + conversion — **[want] lane** (last non-bug cycle `hub-itemlist-jsonld` pulled [goal]; last cycle PASS so no blocker → [want] owed per the 1:1). This is the directly-queued "Next" from the `partnership-seo-alert-capture` cycle ("add the same capture box to `/partnerships/near/[icao]` (the third partnership geo family) for parity") — the aircraft side and the partnership make/state hubs were already done; the near-airport geo family was the remaining gap. A conversion/list-building win the pageview metric can't see tonight. Scoreboard at orient: 148 pageviews last 7d (GSC not configured; STAGE=INDEXING).

## 2026-06-23T10:32Z — PASS — hub-itemlist-jsonld
- Pages: /aircraft, /partnerships
- What: **Added ItemList structured data to the two main marketplace hub pages — Planes for Sale (`/aircraft`) and Aircraft Partnerships (`/partnerships`).** These are the human's priority seed pages #2 and #3, but until now they emitted **no structured data at all**, even though every page below them (make, make+model, state hubs) already tells Google "this is a list of N real aircraft/partnership offers." Now each hub emits an `ItemList` JSON-LD block describing exactly the listings shown on the page (60 aircraft, 23 partnerships at QA time), so search engines understand the two most important pages on the site as genuine marketplace result lists. Invisible head-of-page metadata only — the pages look and behave identically.
- Goal: SEO / structured-data parity on the priority seed hubs (INDEXING stage) — **[goal] lane** (last non-bug cycle `home-newest-partnerships-rail` pulled [want]; last cycle PASS so no blocker → [goal] owed per the 1:1). STAGE=INDEXING, so richer machine understanding of the two top-priority hub pages (seed set #2 + #3) is a leading-indicator win, not a tonight-pageview play. Closes a real gap: the sub-family pages (`/aircraft/[make]`, `/aircraft/[make]/[model]`, `/aircraft/for-sale/[state]`, `/partnerships/make/[make]`, `/partnerships/state/[state]`) all emit ItemList already; the hubs they roll up to did not. Reuses the existing, proven `buildAircraftItemListJsonLd` / `buildPartnershipItemListJsonLd` helpers (same convention, same `application/ld+json` pattern) — no new dependency, no schema/DB change, no fabricated fields (the helpers null-out unpriced/invalid rows). Scoreboard at orient: 148 pageviews last 7d (GSC not configured; STAGE=INDEXING).

- Verdict: PASS. ## 2026-06-23T08:35Z — PASS — alerts-double-opt-in
- Pages: /alerts/status, /aircraft (the alert-signup box), plus two new backend routes (/api/alerts/confirm, /api/alerts/unsubscribe)
- What: **Email alerts now use a proper double-opt-in flow — sign up, get a confirmation email, click to confirm, and a working one-click unsubscribe.** Until now, when a visitor entered their email to get alerts for new listings (the "Get alerts for new Cessna 172 listings" box on the for-sale pages), the address was just stored as "pending" with no way to confirm it or opt back out — so we could never actually, responsibly send a single alert. This cycle wires the real flow: a new signup now triggers a confirmation email with a "Confirm my alerts" button and an unsubscribe link; clicking confirm flips the subscription to **confirmed**, clicking unsubscribe flips it to **unsubscribed**, and both land on a clean branded ClubHanger page telling the visitor what happened. The signup box's success message now says "Almost there — check your inbox" instead of implying they're already subscribed. **Nothing actually sends yet** — the email layer is built to send via Resend the moment the human drops in a `RESEND_API_KEY`, and until then every send is a safe logged no-op (so this ships with zero risk of mailing anyone prematurely).
- Goal: feature depth / conversion infrastructure — **[want] lane** (last non-bug cycle `airport-og-card-parity` pulled [goal]; last cycle PASS so no blocker, so [want] was owed per the 1:1). This is **slice 2** of the top **[P1][want] "Email alerts capture"** item; the backlog explicitly says "Build slices 2-3 NOW, gated behind `RESEND_API_KEY` — do NOT block on the key... no-op + log when it's absent," and the double-opt-in schema (`confirm_token`/`confirmed_at`/`unsubscribe_token`) is already migrated. Slice 1 (capture UI + pending insert) shipped earlier. A list-building / conversion win the pageview metric can't see tonight; it's the prerequisite that makes the list legally sendable (CAN-SPAM/GDPR confirmed opt-in + one-click unsubscribe). Honesty-rule-clean: no fabricated content, no actual sends without a key, soft-fails on bad tokens. Scoreboard at orient: 148 pageviews last 7d (GSC not configured; STAGE=INDEXING).

## 2026-06-23T08:01Z — PASS — clubhanger-estimate-detail
- Pages: /aircraft/listing/[id]
- What: **Each for-sale aircraft's own page now shows a "ClubHanger Estimate" — how its asking price compares to the going rate for the same make+model.** Right under the price, a new panel reads the median asking price of every *other* active, priced listing of the same make+model family and tells the buyer, in one line, whether this plane is asking **Below market / Around market / Above market** — e.g. "Above market · Asking $49,900 (40%) above the median Cessna 172 listing", with the comp count and median shown ("Based on the median asking price of N other Cessna 172 listings for sale now") and a link to see the whole family. It's deliberately a **descriptive market comparison, not a "good deal" endorsement**: the comp set is the entire make+model family, so a big gap usually reflects year/hours/avionics rather than a bargain — the panel says exactly that ("actual value also depends on year, hours, and avionics. An estimate, not an appraisal or an offer"). The block only appears when the listing has a real price AND there are at least 4 other priced same-family comps; on no-price, unknown-family, or thin-data listings it simply doesn't render.
- Goal: feature depth / buyer UX (Zillow "Zestimate" analog) — **[want] lane** (last non-bug cycle `home-rail-cards-internal-link` pulled [goal]; last cycle PASS so no blocker, so [want] was owed per the 1:1). ## 2026-06-23T07:31Z — PASS — listing-cost-and-price-history
- Pages: /aircraft/listing/[id]
- What: **Each for-sale aircraft's own page now shows an "Estimated cost to own" and (when the price has actually moved) a "Price history" block** — the Zillow/Redfin pattern the backlog asks for. The **cost-to-own** block gives a buyer a quick, honest ballpark of what owning the plane outright runs per month/year: insurance (≈1% of the asking price, the one line that scales with this specific aircraft), plus clearly-labeled *typical* figures for hangar/tie-down, the annual inspection, and operating (fuel + reserves at ~$150/hr over an assumed 75 hrs/yr). It carries a plain "rough estimate — your costs will vary" disclaimer and a link to the full cost calculator so buyers can plug in their own numbers — nothing is presented as listing-specific that isn't. The **price-history** block only appears when we have a real recorded price change: it shows the change date, the new price, the signed delta + % (e.g. "−$5,000 (−4%)"), and the original price struck through; listings with no recorded change show no block (no empty filler). No-price listings show neither.
- Goal: feature depth / buyer UX (Zillow/Redfin parity) — **[want] lane** (last non-bug cycle `aircraft-listing-sitemap` pulled [goal]; last cycle PASS so no blocker, so [want] was owed per the 1:1). This is **slice 2** of the top **[P1][want] "Internal listing detail pages"** item (slice 1 = the page; slice 4's sitemap half already shipped). A product win the pageview metric can't see tonight; honesty-rule-clean — the price history is 100% real stored data (`previous_price`/`price_changed_at`), and the cost figure is a transparent, disclosed rule-of-thumb estimate (the cited Zillow "estimated payment" analog), not fabricated content. Scoreboard at orient: 148 pageviews last 7d (GSC not configured; STAGE=INDEXING).

Second, the real fix to the part that *was* a problem (the error being *hidden*): the site previously had **no custom error page at all**, so any unexpected error fell back to a blank/broken default. It now shows a friendly branded "Something went wrong" page (warning icon, a "Try again" button, and a "Go home" link, inside the normal nav + footer) — and the underlying error is now logged instead of swallowed. Nothing about any normal page changed.

Two additive files only — `src/app/error.tsx` (client segment boundary: branded fallback inside the root layout, `reset()` "Try again" + home link, logs the error + shows its `digest`) and `src/app/global-error.tsx` (root-layout boundary with its own inline-styled `<html>`/`<body>`; makes the app **own** the `global-error` build chunk instead of relying on Next's default — the default's chunk is exactly what went missing as the `ChunkLoadError` that masked the real error). ## 2026-06-22T12:32Z — PASS — sitemap-lastmod
- Pages: /sitemap.xml (affects the lastmod of /, /aircraft, /partnerships, all make/model/state/near/airport programmatic pages)
- What: **Every programmatic and index page in our sitemap now carries a real "last updated" date, so Google has a genuine freshness signal it can use to decide what to re-crawl.** Until now only individual partnership listings had a date; the homepage, `/aircraft`, `/partnerships`, and all ~250 make/model/state/near-airport/airport landing pages had none at all. This cycle each of those pages gets an honest `<lastmod>` derived from when its underlying listings actually changed — the aircraft-for-sale pages use the newest for-sale-listing date, the partnership pages use the newest partnership-update date, and the homepage uses the later of the two. The date reflects real data changes (it stays put across deploys when nothing changed), so it's a truthful signal, not fake daily churn. The static guides/tools/about pages deliberately get **no** date (we don't fake a "freshly updated" stamp on copy that didn't change). Nothing about how any page looks or behaves changed — this is pure sitemap/SEO metadata.
- Goal: [goal] — "[P2][goal] Sitemap `lastmod` + crawler ping" (Brainstorm 2026-06-20 §A), the `lastmod` half (crawler-ping-on-deploy half deferred — it touches deploy hooks). Pulled the [goal] lane: the last non-bug cycle (seeker-anonymous-contact) was [want] PASS with no blocker, so [goal] was owed per the 1:1. Top INDEXING-stage value: a real per-page freshness signal helps Google prioritize re-crawl of the ~250 live programmatic URLs that previously carried no date. Judged by leading indicators per the honesty rule (real, data-derived lastmod now live on the programmatic + index URLs; not gameable per-deploy), not tonight's pageview delta. Scoreboard at orient: STAGE=INDEXING (GSC not configured this run; PostHog pageviews 117 last 7d).
- Spec: nightshift/specs/2026-06-22T12-32Z-sitemap-lastmod.md
- Verdict: PASS. One file (`src/app/sitemap.ts`), additive/metadata-only. ## 2026-06-22T11:17Z — PASS — airport-thinpage-prune
- Pages: /airports/[icao] (all airport hub pages), /sitemap.xml
- What: **Stopped ~16,800 near-empty airport pages from polluting our sitemap and Google's index.** We have one hub page per airport (`/airports/KXXX`) for all ~16,885 airports in the database, but only **9** airports actually have an aircraft partnership based there — every other one was a thin, near-identical "No active partnerships based at KXXX yet — Post the first one" page. Until now **all 16,885** were listed in our sitemap as high-priority daily-crawl URLs. That's exactly the kind of thin/doorway-page sprawl Google penalizes, and at our current stage (almost nothing indexed yet) it wastes the crawl budget we want spent on the ~200 pages that actually have content. This cycle: the sitemap now lists **only** airport pages that have a real partnership based there (down from 16,885 to 9 airport URLs; total sitemap 263 URLs), and every other airport page is now marked **"noindex, follow"** — it still loads normally and all its links still work (so Google keeps following them), it just won't be indexed as a thin page. The airport pages that DO have listings (e.g. Palo Alto / KPAO) are completely unchanged and stay fully indexable. Nothing about how any page looks or behaves changed — this is pure SEO hygiene.
- Goal: [goal] — `[P1][goal] Thin-page pruning` (Brainstorm 2026-06-20 §A), the airport family (the biggest thin family by far). Pulled the [goal] lane: the last non-bug cycle (marketplace-cross-sell) was [want] PASS with no blocker, so [goal] was owed per the 1:1. Top INDEXING-stage lever right now — concentrates crawl budget on real content instead of ~16.8k near-duplicate empties; completes the inventory-gating pattern every other programmatic family (make/model/state/near) already had. Judged by leading indicators per the honesty rule (sitemap shrank to inventory-backed URLs; thin pages now noindex,follow), not tonight's pageview delta. ## 2026-06-22T07:08Z — PASS — soft-save-merge-on-login
- Pages: all pages (global) · /saved · /aircraft · /partnerships (anywhere a logged-out "soft save" can happen, then merged on login)

Now, the moment that person signs in or creates an account, those device saves are **automatically copied into their real account** and the device-only copy is cleared — so they keep everything, synced. A small "N saved listings added to your account" confirmation appears so it's not silent. The merge is safe to run twice (it never duplicates a listing you already saved), and a signed-in user with nothing saved on the device sees nothing at all.

## 2026-06-22T02:23Z — PASS — fix-visitor-webhook-204
- Pages: /aircraft, /, /partnerships (all pages — the bug fired on every page load)
- What: **Fixed a bug that was throwing a server error on every single page load across the whole site.** The real-time "visitor radar" feature (the one that pings Slack when someone visits) has a tiny beacon that every visitor's browser calls on each page. When the Slack credentials aren't set in an environment (which is the case on staging/preview), that beacon was crashing with a 500 error — because it tried to send a "204 No Content" response *with* a body, which isn't allowed. Every visitor was silently logging a red 500 error in their browser console on every page. The fix returns a proper empty 204 instead, so the beacon quietly does nothing when Slack isn't configured (exactly as intended) and the console stays clean. The Slack-alerting behavior, when credentials *are* set (production), is completely unchanged.
- Goal: **[bug] / blocker (uncapped, fixed first).** Not the planned lane pick: this cycle was owed **[want]** (last non-bug cycle, partnership-make-faq, was [goal]), and I had the [want] follow-up — removable active-filter chips on /aircraft — built and green. But QA surfaced this pre-existing sitewide 500 console error, which the allocation policy says to fix **before** anything else (a console error is a blocker) — and critically it was breaking the mandatory QA "zero app-origin console errors" gate for *every* cycle going forward, so it had to land first. The deferred filter-chips work is preserved on branch `night/aircraft-filter-chips` (build-green) for the next [want] cycle. Scoreboard at orient: STAGE=INDEXING (GSC not configured this run), pageviews 114/7d.
- Spec: nightshift/specs/20260622T022343Z-fix-visitor-webhook-204.md
- Verdict: PASS. One line of app code changed in `src/app/api/visitor-webhook/route.ts`: the not-configured early return `NextResponse.json({ ok: false }, { status: 204 })` (which throws `TypeError: Invalid response status code 204` — a 204 must be body-less — and 500s) became `new NextResponse(null, { status: 204 })`. Root-caused from the server log (`Invalid response status code 204`) + confirmed the beacon source (`src/lib/analytics.ts`) and the unset env (`SLACK_BOT_TOKEN`/`SLACK_VISITOR_CHANNEL_ID`). `npx next build` green ("✓ Compiled successfully in 22.7s", 239/239 static pages); `tsc --noEmit` clean (only the 4 pre-existing `.test.ts` baseline errors, 0 in touched files). QA against the PRODUCTION build (`npx next build` + `npm run start`, NOT `next dev`; killed lingering stale port-3000 servers first):
  - **(1) Beacon fixed:** `POST /api/visitor-webhook` (Slack env unset) → **204** (was **500**), no body. ✓
  - **(2) Smoke PASS exit 0:** `/aircraft`, `/`, `/partnerships` × desktop 1280 + mobile 375 → all HTTP 200, **zero** app-origin console errors (the sitewide 500 is gone — it was present on every page before), **zero** horizontal overflow. ✓
  - **(3) No server-side throw during QA:** 0 `Invalid response status code 204` lines in the server log across the full smoke run. ✓
  - **(4) Looks right:** /aircraft desktop + 375px screenshots confirm listings/photos/sidebar/footer render correctly and unchanged (backend-only fix). ✓
- Screenshots: nightshift/screenshots/fix-visitor-webhook-204/

## 2026-06-20T13:13Z — PASS — aggregate-offer-jsonld
- Pages: /aircraft/[make], /aircraft/[make]/[model], /aircraft/[make]/[model]/[state]
- What: **Added a page-level price-range "AggregateOffer" to the structured data (JSON-LD) on the for-sale aggregation pages — so Google can show a price range (e.g. "$55,000–$325,000") in the search result.** Each make / make+model / make+model-in-state page now emits one extra invisible `<script type="application/ld+json">` block: a `Product` for the model/make family (named exactly like the page, e.g. "Cessna 172 for sale") whose `offers` is a schema.org `AggregateOffer` with `lowPrice` (cheapest), `highPrice` (priciest), `offerCount` (how many priced listings), and `priceCurrency: "USD"`. **It's computed from real listing data only:** the min/max/count come straight from the listings already shown on the page that have a genuine numeric asking price. Listings priced "Make offer" / "Call" are ignored, never guessed. **Anti-slop guard:** if a page has fewer than 2 priced listings, NO AggregateOffer is emitted at all — we never fabricate or show a degenerate one-price "range." The existing `ItemList`/`Product`/`Offer` markup is untouched and still present. This is invisible markup: zero visual/UI change. NO schema/DB change, NO SQL — read-only.
- Goal: Rich structured data / price-range rich-result eligibility (**Lane [goal]**). Scoreboard at orient = **61** pageviews/7d. Leading indicator: the three for-sale aggregation families (make / make+model / make+model-in-state) are now eligible for Google price-range rich results (higher SERP CTR), real-data-only (min/max/count from listings with a numeric asking_price > 0), with a <2-priced null guard so no fabricated range is ever emitted. New exported helper `buildAircraftAggregateOfferJsonLd` reuses the SAME family name/url each page already passes to the ItemList builder, so the markup can't diverge from the visible page (no cloaking).

- Verdict: PASS. Unit tests: **10/10 pass** (new: correct low/high/count; count reflects only priced listings; returns null with <2 priced — covers 1-priced, 0-priced, empty). **QA against the PRODUCTION build (`npx next build` + `npm run start`, NOT `next dev`), /browse + curl at desktop (1280) + 375px mobile:**
  - **(a) Real make+model page → both blocks present + numbers match:** `/aircraft/cessna/172` returns **200**; served HTML contains the original `ItemList` (numberOfItems=40) AND a new `Product`/`AggregateOffer` with `name`="Cessna 172 for sale", `lowPrice`=55000, `highPrice`=325000, `offerCount`=36, `priceCurrency`="USD". ## 2026-06-20T13:08Z — PASS — robots-hardening
- Pages: /robots.txt
- What: **Tightened `robots.txt` so search crawlers stop wasting crawl budget on internal, private, and duplicate pages.** Previously only `/partnerships/new` was blocked, leaving the admin dashboard, API endpoints, auth/login pages, the private "Saved" and "Searches" user surfaces, the interactive "Compare" tool, and the "post a seeking listing" form all crawlable. Now all of those are explicitly disallowed, while every real content route stays fully crawlable — the homepage, all `/aircraft*` listing and programmatic pages (make / make+model / model-in-state / state / near-airport), `/partnerships*` content pages, `/airports*`, `/guides*`, `/tools*`, and `/about`. ## 2026-06-20T10:33Z — PASS — guide-pre-purchase-inspection
- Pages: /guides/aircraft-pre-purchase-inspection (new), /guides (hub now 6 cards), /guides/how-to-find-aircraft-partners (reciprocal link added)
- What: Shipped a **sixth pillar content guide** — and the **first buyer-side one**: **"Aircraft Pre-Purchase Inspection — A Buyer's Checklist"** at `/guides/aircraft-pre-purchase-inspection`. All 5 existing guides are partnership/co-ownership focused (how co-ownership works, cost, the agreement, leaseback vs co-ownership, finding partners); **none covered the buyer / for-sale side**. This new guide fills that gap and targets the high-intent buyer query "pre-buy / pre-purchase inspection checklist / what to check when buying a used airplane," then **funnels to `/aircraft`** (the highest-traffic marketplace section, which had zero guides pointing into it — its primary CTA is "Browse planes for sale"). Content is genuine, accurate buyer guidance: what a pre-buy covers and why it matters; the six major areas to check (logbooks & AD compliance, engine compression/oil analysis, airframe & corrosion, avionics, paperwork/title & liens, damage history); how to choose an **independent A&P/IA** inspector who works for the buyer; how to think about scope and cost (qualitative ranges only — **no fabricated dollar figures or statistics**); and the red flags. **Honesty rules respected:** no fake precision, no specific legal/airworthiness determinations, and the standard amber "general educational info — not legal/tax/financial/**airworthiness** advice; consult a qualified A&P/IA and your own advisors" disclaimer the other guides use. It is a **distinct topic, not a rephrasing** of the partnership guides. **Wired into the link graph both directions:** the guide links OUT to `/aircraft` (primary CTA), the cost + find-partners guides, and the `/guides` hub; and a **reciprocal `<Link>`** to it was added to the find-partners guide's "Keep reading" block so it's not an orphan. Registered everywhere the others are: the **GUIDES array** (hub card grid + ItemList JSON-LD auto-grow to 6, lucide `ClipboardCheck` icon), **`sitemap.ts`** (priority 0.6, matching the others), and the **Footer `guideLinks`**. NO schema/DB change — additive only.

## 2026-06-20T10:17Z — PASS — forsale-market-snapshot
- Pages: /aircraft/[make]/[model]
- What: Added a tasteful **"Market snapshot"** content block to the make+model for-sale pages (e.g. `/aircraft/cessna/172`) showing **real aggregate price stats** for THAT make+model family, computed from the live `aircraft_for_sale` inventory: the **median asking price**, the **average**, the **lowest** and **highest** asking price, and **how many priced listings** the figures are based on ("From 36 priced Cessna 172 listings on the market right now"). This is **slice 2** of the price-vs-market insight (slice 1 was the per-card "vs market" pill) — it surfaces the **aggregate** market picture as unique, indexable, genuinely-useful content on an existing top-traffic page (no new/thin/doorway page). **Honesty guardrail (built in):** the block renders **only when the family has ≥ 8 priced listings**. This is the same honesty philosophy as slice 1 but a notch stricter on purpose — the snapshot publishes a public **median AND a low–high range**, and a price range is far more outlier-sensitive than a single per-card "below/above" claim. With only ~5 listings, one mis-priced/project airframe skews everything (a real example: Robinson R44 has a $105k listing sitting against a $650k–$860k field). ≥8 cleanly separates the dense families (Cessna 172=36 priced, Cherokee=23, Bonanza=58, Mooney M20=53, Cirrus SR22=158, Cessna 182=38) from sparse ones (Robinson R44=5 → **shows no snapshot at all**, rather than a noisy/misleading aggregate). Prices show as whole dollars (`$127,475`) — no fake precision, no "k" rounding that would hide the real figure; a disclosure line states these are **asking** prices of active listings (not sale prices) and that unpriced listings are excluded. **NO schema/DB change** — additive, read-only, reuses the exact same `aircraft_for_sale` query shape (`status='active'` + `make`/`modelPattern`/`notModelPattern`) the page already uses for its count/state-rail/listing queries. Sky-blue accent on the median (headline) card only; the other three are neutral slate; mobile-first 2-col grid.
- Goal: feature depth + unique market content ([goal] lane) — a real, linkable aggregate "what does a Cessna 172 cost?" answer makes each make+model page substantively more useful and indexable for high-intent queries (GOAL.md `[goal]` SEO/content lever). Slice 2 of the "price-vs-market insight" item. Lane **[goal]** — **deliberate fall-through**: the prior non-bug cycle (forsale-vs-market-pill) was also `[goal]`, but the `[want]` lane is currently exhausted/blocked (email-alerts slice 1 shipped, slices 2/3 need transactional-email infra; trust-layer + similar-listings done on partnerships and blocked for for-sale; filter overhaul / available+seeking / compatibility / pilot-profiles all blocked or thrash-risky), so per GOAL.md "if the chosen lane is empty, fall through to the other." Scoreboard at orient = **61** pageviews/7d.
- How: EDIT **`src/lib/aircraftComps.ts`** — new pure, no-DB/no-React `priceStats(prices: number[]): PriceStats | null` (count/median/low/high/average, whole-dollar rounded; returns null below `MIN_SNAPSHOT_LISTINGS=8`); reuses the file's existing median logic. EDIT **`src/components/AircraftSaleList.tsx`** — new exported server helper `priceStatsForMakeModel(make, modelPattern, notModelPattern)` mirroring `topStatesForMakeModel`'s query shape (selects only `asking_price`, narrowed to active priced listings, `.limit(5000)`; non-fatal → null on any failure) and calling `priceStats`. EDIT **`src/app/aircraft/[make]/[model]/page.tsx`** — fetch the stats once, render the "Market snapshot" `<section>` (gated on non-null) between the specs/cost-to-own cards and the email-alert signup; added a `fmtUsd` whole-dollar formatter. **NO parallel duplicate inventory query** (reuses the page's existing family query shape); no JSON-LD AggregateOffer added (the existing ItemList marks up only the first page of listings, so a full-family AggregateOffer would be inconsistent — skipped per spec "if unsure, skip"); no frozen file touched.

## 2026-06-20T10:05Z — PASS — forsale-vs-market-pill
- Pages: /aircraft, /aircraft/[make]/[model], /aircraft/for-sale/[state]
- What: Added a small, honest **"vs market" pill** to the planes-for-sale cards. For a listing with a real asking price, it compares that price to the **median asking price of OTHER active for-sale listings of the same make+model family** and shows a sky/emerald **"~X% below average"** (good for a buyer), a neutral slate **"~X% above average"**, or a neutral **"Near average"** (within ±5% of the median, so we don't claim fake precision on what's basically the going rate). The pill carries a small line-chart icon and lives in the card's **badges row** — so it never overlaps the heart/Save button or the Compare toggle (both verified non-overlapping at desktop + 375px). Because all three for-sale surfaces render the same card/list, the badge appears across **`/aircraft`, the make+model pages (e.g. `/aircraft/cessna/172`), and the by-state pages** at once. **Honesty guardrail built into the feature:** the pill renders **only when there are ≥ 4 OTHER priced comps** in the same family (≥ 5 priced listings including the listing itself). Below that threshold — and for any listing with **no asking price**, or a make+model that doesn't resolve to a known family — it shows **nothing** (never a fake/empty/misleading badge). Verified live: a dense family (`/aircraft/cessna/172`, 40 cards / 36 priced) shows 36 sensible pills — a $75k listing reads "~42% below average" (emerald), a $325k one reads "~160% above average" (slate); a sparse family (`/aircraft/robinson/r44`, 6 cards) shows **0 pills**. **NO schema/DB change** — additive, read-only computation from the existing `aircraft_for_sale` inventory the make+model pages already query. Sky-blue/emerald accent only; mobile-first; no dark patterns, no fake precision.
- Goal: feature depth + unique/shareable market data ([goal] lane) — a real, linkable "below/above market" signal makes the for-sale pages more useful and share-worthy than a bare aggregator listing (GOAL.md `[goal]` SEO/shareability lever). Slice 1 of the "price-vs-market insight" backlog item. Lane **[goal]**; scoreboard at orient = **61** pageviews/7d. Prior non-bug cycle (saved-aircraft-view) pulled `[want]`, so this correctly pulls `[goal]` per the 1:1 alternation.
- How: NEW **`src/lib/aircraftComps.ts`** — pure, no-DB/no-React helpers: `buildFamilyPriceMap(listings)` buckets `{make,model,asking_price}` rows into a family→sorted-prices map keyed by the existing `resolveMakeModelFamily` (the same single source of truth the card already uses for its "See all … for sale" link); `compVsMarket(listing, map)` excludes exactly one occurrence of the listing's own price, requires `MIN_OTHER_COMPS=4` others, computes the median, applies the `DEAD_BAND=0.05` near-average window, and rounds the percent (no decimals; clamped ≥1 just outside the band). EDIT **`src/components/AircraftSaleList.tsx`** — one extra lightweight read (`make, model, asking_price` for active priced listings, `.limit(5000)`, mirrors `topStatesForMakeModel`; non-fatal → empty map on any failure), built once and `Promise.all`'d alongside the existing saved-ids read, then `compVsMarket(p, map)` passed per card. EDIT **`src/components/AircraftSaleCard.tsx`** — accept a `comp?: CompResult | null` prop and render a `CompPill` in the badges row (emerald for below, slate for above/near), right after the price-drop badge so price signals group together. No new route, no frozen file touched, additive only.
- Spec: nightshift/specs/20260620T100524Z-forsale-vs-market-pill.md
- Verdict: PASS. `npx next build` green; `npx tsc --noEmit`: only the 3 pre-existing `.test.ts` import-extension baseline errors (aircraftJsonLd/calculators/partnershipTrust) — **no new errors in any touched file**. **QA against the PRODUCTION build (`npm run start`, NOT `next dev`), driven with /browse at desktop (1280) + 375px mobile:**
  - **(a) Comp math correct on a real dense family** (`/aircraft/cessna/172`): 36 priced cards all show a sensible pill; spot-checks — $75,000 → "~42% below average" (emerald), $89,995 → "~31% below average", $325,000 → "~160% above average" (slate), a mid listing → "Near average". Below/above classification + percentages match `median(others)` by inspection.
  - **(b) Sparse-family + no-price guardrail** (`/aircraft/robinson/r44`, 6 cards): **0 pills** rendered — the ≥4-others threshold suppresses the badge rather than showing a misleading one. "Contact for price" listings (no `asking_price`) and unresolved make+models (Hangar, Bombardier 7500, Diamond DA42) correctly get no pill on `/aircraft` (68 priced/resolved cards got a pill, 32 unresolved/unpriced got none).

## 2026-06-20T08:55Z — PASS — compare-aircraft
- Pages: /aircraft, /compare
- What: Shipped **SLICE 2 of listing comparison — the planes-for-sale marketplace**. Every for-sale card on **`/aircraft`** now gets the same sky **"Compare" toggle** that partnerships got tonight, wired into the **SAME compare tray** (fixed bottom bar with removable chips, `N/3` counter, Clear, and a "Compare (N)" button) — no fork, no duplicate system. Clicking "Compare (N)" opens **`/compare?type=aircraft&ids=…`**, a **side-by-side table** of 2–3 aircraft with REAL for-sale fields only: make, model, year, price (asking or text), total time (TTAF), SMOH, engine, annual due, damage history, avionics, location/state, registration, source (`—` when a listing lacks a field). **Each column links to the listing's real destination** — the original source listing (e.g. the aircraftforsale.com page, opens in a new tab), or, if a listing has no source URL, the matching make+model for-sale page — **never an invented detail route** (for-sale aircraft have no detail page on the site). **The two marketplaces never mix:** selection is scoped to ONE listing type at a time — if you've got aircraft in the tray and click Compare on a partnership (or vice-versa), the prior selection is **replaced** (obvious, no silent merge of planes-and-partnerships into one nonsensical table). Selection stays **client-side only** (React + `sessionStorage`, hydrated after mount), **NO DB / schema change**. Graceful for **both** types: 0 → "Choose … to compare", 1 (or 1 real + bogus ids) → "Pick one more … to compare", >3 → capped at 3 (deduped); invalid ids silently dropped. `/compare` stays **noindex** and out of the sitemap.

## 2026-06-20T07:38Z — PASS — email-alerts
- Pages: /aircraft/[make]/[model], /aircraft/for-sale/[state]
- ⚠️ SCHEMA CHANGE: added table `alerts` ⚠️ — STRICTLY ADDITIVE (`create table if not exists alerts (...)`), NOTHING dropped/altered/deleted/truncated, no existing table touched. Applied to the SHARED prod+staging Supabase (project `aeromatch` / khypdoyfhwtdwaelzzle) via `apply_migration` (name `add_alerts_table`) and mirrored into `supabase/schema.sql`. RLS mirrors the existing `waitlist` table: **anon can INSERT (no account required) but there is NO public SELECT** — `alerts_anyone_insert` (`with check (true)`) + `alerts_service_read` (`auth.role() = 'service_role'`), so visitor emails (PII) are NOT readable by anon/other users (verified: anon REST SELECT → `[]`). Columns: `id uuid pk`, `email text not null`, `context text`, `source_path text`, `status text not null default 'pending'`, `created_at timestamptz default now()`, `unique(email, source_path)` + a `status` index. The Supabase security advisor flags `alerts_anyone_insert` as "RLS Policy Always True" — EXPECTED and intentional, identical to the existing `waitlist`/`feedback`/`partnerships` anon-insert policies (it's the "anyone can submit, no account" design; PII is protected by the absence of a public SELECT, not by the insert check).
- What: Added a tasteful, low-friction **inline email-alerts capture** (slice 1 of the [P1][want] Email alerts feature) to the two highest-intent programmatic for-sale pages we shipped tonight, so the growing SEO traffic can opt into "tell me when a new one is listed." It is **inline, NOT a modal/popup, with no fake urgency** (FREEZE/taste rule): a single email field + a "Get alerts" button in a sky-blue card, with **contextual copy that names the make/model or state**. On `/aircraft/[make]/[model]` (e.g. `/aircraft/cessna/172`) it reads "Get alerts for new **Cessna 172** listings"; on `/aircraft/for-sale/[state]` (e.g. `/aircraft/for-sale/california`) it reads "Get alerts for new **California** listings". **No account required.** On submit it persists the email + context (the make/model or state) + the source path into the new `alerts` table with `status='pending'` + `created_at`, then shows a friendly success state in-place ("You're on the list. We'll email you when new {X} listings appear. No spam — just relevant aircraft."). Basic email-format validation rejects bad input gracefully with an inline message (no crash, no row written). **Dedupe is idempotent**: submitting the same email+context twice is a no-op success, not an error. This is the waitlist seed — `status='pending'` is the seam for slice 2's double-opt-in confirmation.
- Goal: feature depth / conversion — seed an email list off the growing SEO traffic (the [P1][want] "Email alerts capture" backlog item). Lane **[want]**; scoreboard at orient = **54** (scoreboard prints 60 pageviews/7d). (Most recent non-bug cycle was `[goal]` (make-model-expand), so this correctly pulls `[want]` per the 1:1 alternation; and it's the explicit slice-1 the human scoped.)
- How: NEW `src/components/AlertSignup.tsx` — a `'use client'` inline form (single email input + button → friendly success/error states, sky-blue accent ONLY, no emerald/other palettes, no modal). NEW server action `subscribeToAlerts(email, context, sourcePath)` in `src/app/actions.ts` mirroring the existing `joinWaitlist` (anon insert via the cookie-bound server client). **Key implementation detail:** I started with `.upsert(... onConflict)` like `joinWaitlist`, but PostgREST upsert needs SELECT to detect conflicts and the table is insert-only for anon (no SELECT policy, to protect PII) → the upsert 401'd with RLS error 42501. Fixed by switching to a **plain `.insert()` and swallowing the `23505` unique-violation** as an idempotent success — keeps RLS minimal (insert-only = strongest PII protection) AND gives graceful dedupe. EDIT both page files: import + render `<AlertSignup context={label|entry.name} sourcePath={path} />` (after the specs/cost grid on make+model; after the header on state). - How: NEW `getInventoryMakeModels()` in `src/lib/seo.ts` — the **SINGLE source of truth** shared by `generateStaticParams`, the sitemap, and `resolveMakeModel` so they can never drift. It reads `make, model` from `aircraft_for_sale` (status='active') via a **cookieless anon read client** (build-safe inside `generateStaticParams`/sitemap where `cookies()` would throw), normalizes each row to a clean make-slug + **family** model-slug using the SAME slug conventions slice 1 uses (cessna/172, cirrus/sr22), and **handles messy data**: skips null/blank make or model; skips a denylist of non-manufacturer "makes" (experimental, biplane, amphibian, hangar, land, single family, other, piston/turbine helicopter, …); collapses Cirrus SR G-suffix variants into sr20/sr22/sr22t; strips trailing variant letters on number models (182p→182, 172m→172); drops junk family tokens. It groups by make+family, keeps families with **count ≥ 3** (substantive, no thin/singleton pages), then **dedupes** so a narrower family that's a strict prefix-subset of a broader one is dropped (no m20j page when m20 exists) and a dynamic family that duplicates a curated one by the SAME make+pattern is dropped (no `grumman/aa1` clashing with curated `grumman/aa-1` — both match `aa1%`). Curated entries always win on collision. Dynamic-only families get **generic, honest** specs/cost-to-own copy (no fabricated specifics). NEW async `resolveMakeModel(makeSlug, modelSlug)` — curated match first (sync), else the inventory-backed set. EDIT `src/app/aircraft/[make]/[model]/page.tsx` — `generateStaticParams` is now async + returns the full set; page + metadata use `resolveMakeModel`; the related-combos rail draws from the merged list. `dynamicParams` stays the default `true` so any valid-but-not-prebuilt combo still renders on demand, and the existing `n===0 → notFound()` guard 404s thin/garbage combos. EDIT `src/app/sitemap.ts` — the make+model section uses `getInventoryMakeModels()` (same set), still gated `count>0` via the existing `countMakeModel`. **Graceful build-time fallback preserved**: any DB failure returns the static `SEO_MAKE_MODELS` rather than crashing the build. **NO schema change, additive only**, no frozen file touched.

## 2026-06-20T07:12Z — PASS — aircraft-jsonld
- Pages: /aircraft/[make]/[model], /aircraft/for-sale/[state]
- What: Shipped **Schema.org JSON-LD structured data on the two new aircraft for-sale SEO pages** so their listings are now eligible for Google **rich results** (= higher CTR = more pageviews on our highest-intent pages). Both `/aircraft/[make]/[model]` (e.g. `/aircraft/cessna/172`) and `/aircraft/for-sale/[state]` (e.g. `/aircraft/for-sale/california`) already had unique titles/H1/meta/canonical + crawlable BreadcrumbList JSON-LD, but the actual for-sale LISTINGS on them carried no product markup. Since there is **no individual aircraft detail page** (these are LIST pages aggregating third-party listings), the markup is modeled as an **`ItemList`** whose items are the for-sale aircraft shown on the page, each a **`Product`** with an **`Offer`** (price, `priceCurrency: USD`, `availability: InStock`, `itemCondition: UsedCondition`, and the listing's real source URL). The markup reflects **only real data**: each item's `name` is the visible card title, its `url` is the listing's real `source_url`, and an `Offer` is attached **only** when the listing has a genuine numeric `asking_price` — listings priced "Make offer"/"Call" get **no** offer rather than a made-up price.
- Goal: SEO breadth/quality — rich-result eligibility (structured data) on the two new high-intent for-sale page families. Lane **[goal]**; scoreboard at orient = **54** (scoreboard prints 60 pageviews/7d). (Prior non-bug cycle was `[want]` (trust-nudges), so this cycle correctly pulls `[goal]` per the 1:1 alternation; and it's the explicit "Vehicle/Offer JSON-LD on the make+model + state pages for rich results" both the aircraft-make-model-pages and aircraft-state-pages cycles flagged as Next.)
- How: NEW `src/lib/aircraftJsonLd.ts` — a **pure** `buildAircraftItemListJsonLd(listings, {name,url})` that maps `AircraftForSale[]` → an `ItemList` of `ListItem`→`Product`/`Offer`, with the **honesty rules baked in**: omits any property we don't have, **never** emits `aggregateRating`/`review` (no real review data exists; fake review markup is a Google penalty + a GOAL.md honesty-rule violation), and **never** emits `image` (the cards render a generic placeholder explicitly labeled "Not actual plane photo", so there's no real per-listing photo to mark up). NEW `src/lib/aircraftJsonLd.test.ts` — 7 unit tests (valid @context/@type, name=card title + url=source_url, numeric price → real USD Offer, no-price → no offer, never-emits aggregateRating/review/image, empty set → null, blank-title skipped). EDIT `src/components/AircraftSaleList.tsx` — extracted + exported `fetchAircraftPage(filters)` (the component now calls it; **single source of truth, no behavior change**) so each page marks up **exactly** the first page of listings the visitor sees (same filters/order). EDIT both page files — `await fetchAircraftPage(...)` then inject the ItemList via a `<script type="application/ld+json">` with `dangerouslySetInnerHTML` of `JSON.stringify(...)`, **matching the repo's existing pattern** (`Breadcrumbs.tsx`, `partnerships/[id]/page.tsx`). **NO schema/DB change, additive only**; diff scoped to the two pages + one shared helper + the list-fetch extraction.

Pure server-rendered links via the existing `pageHref()` helper — no client JS. - Spec: nightshift/specs/2026-06-19T0902Z-aircraft-pagination.md
- Verdict: PASS. `npx next build` green (compile + typecheck). QA via /browse against the live DB (1,856 active listings → 31 pages):
  - Page 1: header "Showing 1–60 of 1,856", pager "← Previous (disabled) | Page 1 of 31 | Next →".
  - `?page=2`: header "Showing 61–120 of 1,856", listings differ from page 1 (page 2 starts "Cirrus Sf50 G2 Plus" vs page 1 "Hangar Airport Boulevard…"), Previous href = `/aircraft` (drops page param), Next href = `/aircraft?page=3`.
  - Filter preservation: `?max_tt=2000&page=2` → header "Showing 61–120 of 418", prev/next hrefs carry `max_tt=2000` (`/aircraft?max_tt=2000`, `/aircraft?max_tt=2000&page=3`).
  - Out-of-range `?page=9999`: graceful "No more aircraft on this page." + "← Back to the first page" link (→ `/aircraft`), NO red error box and no crash. (Caught a bug during QA: PostgREST returns a 416 "range not satisfiable" when the offset is past the end, which the old single `error` flag rendered as the generic "Failed to load… try again" box. Fixed: an error on page > 1 is treated as out-of-range, only page 1 — offset 0, always satisfiable — keeps the genuine error box.)
  - 375px mobile (`?page=2`): no horizontal overflow (scrollWidth = clientWidth = 375), pager wraps cleanly.
  - Console: only the pre-existing Wikimedia LCP image warnings (warnings, not errors) — no new errors.
